- **Generation outages (4/2 actual): 55,107 MW total.** Planned 39,479. Maint **5,356** (-90, continuing to decline from 8,390 peak). **Forced 10,272** (-335). 4-day forced trajectory: 10,056 → 10,607 → 10,272 — **locked at ~10 GW.** The 06b forecast of 6,815 was a false signal. Forced outage floor is 10 GW.
- **Transmission — returning 500+ kV:**
  - **TODAY:** Chancelr TX4 500 kV (DOM-C), Brighton XFMR 500 kV (PEP, same-day)
  - **TOMORROW 4/3: MAJOR RETURN DAY.** 765 kV **Marquis2 XF1 (AEP-OH, slipped from 3/31 → 4/1 → NOW 4/3 — 60 days out!)**. 500 kV **Limerick-Whitpain (PE)** + **Brunsswy-Rogersrd (DOM-C)**. Multiple ComEd 345 kV. **Marquis2 has slipped twice — flagging risk of further delay.**
  - **4/8:** Juniata-Keystone 500 kV (PL-S, extended from 4/5 to 4/8)
- **Still active (month-long):** Ladysmith-Elmont4 500 kV (DOM-C, → 4/30), Deans-Smithbur 500 kV (PS-N, → 5/15), Possumpt corridor 2 × 500 kV (→ 4/29), Fentres4 TX5 XFMR (DOM-E, → 7/18)

  **THE KEY FINDING: HE15 was not just congestion — it was system scarcity.** System energy hit $125.95 at HE15 while WH had +$36.71 cong. Total gen 97,459 MW. The solar cliff (8,279 → 7,521 = -758 MW) hit while load was still rising. Western PJM couldn't get enough power through the constraints OR from its own stack. This is the first hour where system energy exceeded $100 on a weekday in the series.

But Deans-Smithbur (PS-N, 6 weeks) and Ladysmith-Elmont4 (DOM-C, month) keep the base elevated. **Wind building to 8+ GW today should compress congestion significantly from HE14 onward.** With 8.5 GW wind at HE20, the evening ramp should be much smoother.

**Coal 14,670 MW at HE21 is a NEW SERIES HIGH** (prev 13,688 Mon). Coal ramped +3 GW from HE6 to HE21. Gas peaked at 38,936 (below Monday's 40,536 record). **Total thermal HE21: 53,606 MW** (gas 38,936 + coal 14,670). HE19 total gen **99,289 MW — NEW SERIES HIGH.** The system dispatched near-maximum thermal and still needed every MW.

**HE1 overnight: gas 32,275 + coal 13,604 = 45,879 thermal at 1 AM.** This is extremely high for overnight — coal didn't ramp down because it couldn't. The HE24 gas ramp of -5,901 MW is the sharpest single-hour decline in the series, explaining the HE24 price spike (demand dropping faster than gas can cycle off, creating temporary oversupply that reverses into a constraint as flows shift).

### What Matters Today
- **WIND IS THE GAME CHANGER.** Building from 6.5 GW to 8.5+ GW by evening. Yesterday's HE15 $164 happened with 6.5 GW wind. Today's HE15 should have 7.8 GW wind — that's 1.3 GW more cushion at the critical solar cliff. Evening wind at 8.5 GW is back to the HIGH regime that suppressed prices to $56-69 on Mon/Sun.
- **DA $50.17 is closer to fair but still likely rich.** Bias-adj estimate $45.83. Yesterday's $64.49 DA → $57.27 RT (-$7.22). The $50 DA with stronger renewables should produce RT ~$44-48 WH. Midday will be cheaper with more solar (9 GW peak) and more wind.
- **Marquis2 STILL hasn't returned — watch for 4/3 slip again.** Originally scheduled 3/31, slipped to 4/1, now 4/3. If it slips again, the Western PJM constraint persists. 4/3 is also the return date for Limerick-Whitpain and Brunsswy-Rogersrd — a true test of whether the congestion regime breaks.
- **Overnight spikes are the new normal.** HE1 and HE24 both spiked >$80 yesterday. This is a new pattern — the constraint doesn't sleep. Track HE24 tonight and HE1 tomorrow.
- **OnPk est: WH ~$44-48 (bias-adj $45.83).** With wind building and solar recovering, midday should be back to $20-35 WH with Dom suppressed. Evening HE20-21 should be $55-70 with 8+ GW wind. The extreme HE15-type spikes are less likely today.

### Trade Implications / Risk Checks
- **4/3 is the inflection point.** Three major 500 kV returns + Marquis2 765 kV. If these deliver, the congestion regime moderates. WH-EH spread should compress from $17.78 toward $10-12. If Marquis2 slips again, the spread holds.
- **Overnight congestion is mispriced in DA.** DA has overnight (HE1-6) at $24-36 WH, but RT has been printing $57-88. The DA is completely missing the overnight constraint. This is a persistent short opportunity.
- **Dom DA is wrong.** Yesterday DA had Dom at +$0.86 cong (slight premium); RT had -$9.17 (deep discount). Today DA has -$1.62. The market hasn't figured out that Dom flips to discount in RT when the N-S constraint binds. Dom DA is consistently overpriced vs EH DA.
- **Week 1 at $58 still looks reasonable** given forced outages holding at 10 GW and the new outage pipeline (Deans-Smithbur 6 weeks, Ladysmith-Elmont4 month-long).

- **Evening ramp (HE17-20) — ACCELERATING.** HE17: WH $60.02 (+$14.29 cong) — first real spike, solar cliff beginning. HE20: WH $56.46 / Dom $56.57 / EH $55.80 — system energy $55.48, congestion minimal, pure demand.

HE23: Dom $76.99 (+$18.52), EH $23.72 (-$35.16). **The HE22 EH -$46.71 is the most extreme single-hour congestion in the entire run series.** DA had Dom $56.13 / EH $35.78 at HE22 → DARTs: Dom -$54.72 / EH -$5.72. DA completely mispriced the late evening.
- **Biggest drivers:** (1) **HE21-23 late evening blowout.** Gas ramp to 38,507 MW at HE21 + coal ramping 920 MW = 49.8 GW thermal, despite 8.5 GW wind. Total outages 57.3 GW (highest in series) meant the supply stack was tight. (2) **HE10-12 Dom collapse** — sub-$10 pricing with -$15 to -$17 congestion. Solar + wind = 17 GW midday. (3) **HE22 congestion regime shift** — the constraint flipped from energy-driven (HE21, flat congestion) to congestion-driven (HE22, -$46.71 EH) within one hour. Load dropping exposed the N-S constraint.

### Notes

- Gridstatus

The SPC has issued a level 3/5 enhanced risk for much of Western PJM and MISO central this afternoon. Warm air is flowing into the region from the Gulf, which, combined with mostly clear skies, is expected to drive some marginal light cooling load risk.

This warm air is fuel for storms, as it runs into a stationary front over the Great Lakes, fueling the risk for strong storms this afternoon as the two collide. These storms would help to push back on some afternoon cooling risk, though the level of potential demand destruction is nowhere near the level we'd expect during summer.

- Gridstatus

PJM saw additional rounds of volatility this morning as South load increased nearly 500 MW d/d. Isolated price spikes occurred before sunrise as sink-side heating load, paired with generation outages and strong hydro generation on the source drove strong intervals of Nottingham congestion.

While temperatures were not notably cooler d/d, milder daytime conditions yesterday helped to enable a stronger heating response this morning. Models indicate that mornings are expected to grow increasingly mild over the next week, though a warming trend could shift this congestion risk towards the evening as cooling load season emerges and with the loss Surr


- Gridstatus

PJM is likely to capture more N-S congestion in tomorrow's DA and will likely see spikes again tomorrow morning.

Temperatures across Virginia are expected to remain similar tomorrow morning, but notably, daytime temperatures today, especially in Southern Virginia, are expected to be considerably cooler d/d. Yesterday saw some daytime cooling load in the zone, likely limiting the heating load impacts this morning as residual warmth limited this morning's response.

Without this daytime warmth today, and with cool temperatures and clear skies tomorrow AM, we'll likely see more Dominion premium in DA clears


- Gridstatus

PJM's Davis Besse plant could begin to ramp up from its refueling outage tomorrow.

During the plant's last refueling outage, the unit was offline for 25 days, exiting the stack on 3/3/2024 and ramping up over the late evening on 3/28/2024. This cycle, the unit exited the stack on 3/1/26, which could indicate a restart over the next day, if a similar timeline is followed.

The return of this unit would help to reduce the risk of price spikes, which have occurred over the peaks as a result of generators ramping.

### What Matters Today
- **Evening ramp is the most constrained setup in the run series.** 97 GW peak load + 852 MW wind + zero solar + 51.3 GW outages. Sunday's HE21 at 99 GW / 3,000 wind / 49.7 GW outages produced Dom $127 and EH -$58 cong. - **3/27 Wednesday is the pivot date.** Conemaug-Juniata, Clifton-Mosby, Clover TX7, plus 10+ 345 kV outages return. But Hopecreek-Redlion and Burchesh-Possumpt add NJ/PEP corridor risk 3/25-3/26. Congestion rotates, doesn't resolve.

### Trade Implications / Risk Checks
- **DART positioning:** Sunday's OnPk DART was small (-$2 to -$5) despite extreme hourly swings. DA is pricing congestion more accurately now (EH -$19.65 today vs -$15.11 Sun). The DA may be right on average but **hourly dispersion is extreme** — the trade is volatility, not direction. HE20 DART could be +$60 (like Sunday) if DA overprices the evening again.
- **Congestion theme:** EH discount widening 4 straight days. Today's -$19.65 DA congestion is the widest in the run series. If wind underperforms the 852 MW forecast (possible given the steep decline from 3,044 morning), congestion blows out further. **Risk: if wind holds above 1,500 MW at HE20, the EH congestion may be overpriced in the DA.**
- **BalWeek at $40-50 is interesting.** Sunday settled $51.44. If today prints $60+ RT OnPk and tomorrow is similarly constrained (new 500 kV outages), BalWeek at $40 bid looks cheap. But the 3/27 outage return wave could deflate the back half of the week.
- **Week 1 at $54.75-57 is the forward anchor.** Barely moved despite Sunday's fireworks. If this week averages $55+ (plausible with the outage/wind setup), Week 1 is fair. If the outage returns on 3/27 resolve congestion, Week 1 is expensive.

### Trade Implications / Risk Checks

### NOTES

- Gridstatus Nuclear 

The nuclear supply stack had some expected, albeit in some days delayed, changes this weekend.

As expected in PJM, Susquehanna 1 ramped down over the early morning today, reducing baseload supply and partially helping drive some of this morning's energy price volatility.

- Gridstatus MISO

MISO real-time energy prices exceeded $4,484/MWh over the evening ramp on Saturday, March 21st.

Warm temperatures across the footprint drove considerably stronger cooling load than initially forecast. This upside is visible primarily in the afternoon, which indicates a stronger cooling load response rather than another driver, such as cloud coverage.

This load overperformance came at the net load peak, which, combined with over 45 GW of generation outages, led to a sharp spike in energy prices. This price interval did see the highest amount of battery discharging that day

### NOTES

- Gridstatus

Susquehanna 1 is expected to begin a refueling outage on Monday, March. 23rd.

Beyond adding to PJM's challenges in managing price volatility over cool mornings or warm spring evenings, the outage is expected to reduce the risk of bullish N-S congestion.

Calvert Cliffs has returned to the stack on the sink, and the loss of this large baseload unit on the source helps to reduce power flows, though outages

- Gridstatus

Speaking of the Dominion Zone premium over Dominion Hub, two line outages are expected to widen this spread again on Monday.

Outages are scheduled on the Elmont and Chickahominy 500kV network, which is expected to put pressure on constraints like Harrowgate - Locks over the solar hours. S-N constraints like these are bearish to the Hub but bullish to the zone, widening the basis.

One thing to keep an eye on is the risk of pronounced solar curtailments due to negative pricing, which we have seen over the past few weeks with congestion related to outages on the Ladysmith network. This can wind up driving spikes of N-S congestion as well, though the loss of Susquehannah could limit some of this risk.

## 2026-03-19 (Thursday)

### What Matters Today
1. **DA stepped down to $57.72 West — this is the de-escalation call.** Yesterday DA at $90 overpriced by $36. Today DA at $58 with 97 GW flat / 111 GW peak load forecast is pricing a much more realistic day. Meteo system HE20 forecast: $56.58 — essentially in line with DA for once. **The persistent DA overpricing may finally be correcting.**
2. **Wind at extreme lows (1,077 MW forecast at HE20) but load much lighter.** The combination of 1,077 MW wind + 508 MW solar + ~95 GW evening load is fundamentally different from yesterday's 1,200 MW wind + 118 GW load. **Net load at HE20 today ~94 GW vs ~116 GW yesterday.** The supply deficit is 22 GW smaller.
3. **Congestion regime is shifting.** Hosensac-Lausanne 500 kV returned today. HE1 overnight congestion went from -$129 Eastern (yesterday) to -$29 (today). **Tomorrow: Graceton-Manor + Conastone-NW + Cloverd2 765 kV all return.** This is the most significant single-day congestion relief of the entire week. Anyone positioned for N-S congestion beyond today should consider exiting.
4. **Gas stress fully resolved.** M3 at $2.62 (back to pre-cold front $2.47 levels). AGT collapsed -$1.42 to $3.20. This takes ~$2/MWh off the marginal gas unit vs Tuesday's peak. No longer a price driver.
5. **Meteo projection and ECMWF ensemble converged.** The 11 GW divergence that persisted for 5 runs is gone — both agree on ~96-97 GW HE21 peak. Models confident the evening won't blow up (ensemble spread only 1,333 MW at HE20).
6. **BalWeek at $46.75 (covers Friday only)** — collapsed from $61 Tuesday. Market sees Friday as benign with outages returning. Week 1 steady at $58.75.

### Trade Implications / Risk Checks
- **DART today:** DA at $57.72 West with Meteo system $56.58 HE20. If the evening ramp delivers $55-65 West HE20, DARTs will be near zero for the first time all week. **The DA finally seems appropriately priced.** Risk is to the downside if load undershoots the 111 GW PJM forecast — Meteo has HE21 at only 96.5 GW. If Meteo is right, RT flat could print $45-50, yielding a modest +$8-12 DART.
- **Congestion cliff tomorrow:** Graceton + Conastone returning 3/20 = N-S flow relief. Eastern Hub congestion should moderate from -$20 to -$10 or less. Dom congestion premium should compress. **Exit any long N-S congestion positions by end of day.**
- **BalWeek at $46.75 for Friday** — market pricing the outage relief. If Graceton/Conastone return on schedule, Friday should be the softest day of the week. But if any return is delayed, Friday could reprice higher.
- **Week 1 (3/23-27) at $58.75** — with Fentress-Yadkin returning 3/24, next week should see further congestion relief. But Vassell 765 kV XFMR (AEP) starting today through 6/11 and Fentres4 500 kV XFMR (DOM-E) through 7/15 are new long-duration outages that could sustain some constraint pressure.
- **Wind floor risk:** 1,077 MW wind at HE20 is extremely low. If load comes in above Meteo's 95 GW call — even by 3-4 GW — the evening could surprise higher with no wind cushion. But ensemble spread is only 1,333 MW at HE20, so models are confident.
- **Outages climbing (+2 GW DoD to 44.7 GW)** with maint +2.4 GW. Spring outage season accelerating even as the cold event fades. Watch for forced outage surprises as units that ramped hard all week trip.

Solar peaked at 10,716 MW (peak reading). **Dom spent 8 consecutive hours with negative congestion** (HE10-17). DA had priced Dom HE11-16 at $20-48 — still overpriced vs RT's $8-17 range.
- **Evening ramp (HE19-21):** **HE19 lit up: Dom $50.24, West $47.36** as solar cliff hit. **HE20: Dom $129.27 (+$13.89 cong), West $121.77, East $81.38 (-$36.37 cong).** DA had HE20 at Dom $223.90/West $219.41 — **DART +$97/+$94.** DA massively overpriced the evening peak again. **HE21: Dom $101.99, West $93.67** vs DA $200.04/$193.94 — **DART +$98/+$100.** The wind crash materialized (2,800 MW at HE20) but the ramp still didn't reach DA levels. Why? Load peaked at 112,580 — strong but not the 119 GW that DA was pricing. Hydro ramped hard (+5,754 MW at HE20).
- **Late night (HE22-24):** N-S congestion intensified dramatically. **HE24: Dom $81.72 (+$22.36 cong), East $10.80 (-$49.29 cong).** This directly fed into today's HE1 -$129 Eastern congestion. The overnight heating load buildup under Bedington/Graceton constraints creates an N-S pressure cooker.
- **What drove Tuesday's DARTs (+$35 West, +$28 Dom):** (1) **Wind crashed from 9,308 → 4,771 MW** — finally delivered the bearish cushion removal that DA had been pricing all week. (2) But the evening ramp still underdelivered vs DA because load peaked at 112.6 GW, not the 119+ GW DA was pricing. (3) Solar was strong (peak 10,716 MW) creating a deep midday valley that destroyed Dom. (4) **Hydro ramped +5,754 MW at HE20** — partially offset the wind loss. (5) Gas easing (M3 -$0.16) kept marginal costs below DA's assumption.

### What Matters Today
1. **PJM forecasting 119.6 GW peak** — would be +7 GW above yesterday's 112.6 GW. This is the setup that could finally validate the DA. Meteo ECMWF has 108.3 GW HE21, Meteo projection only 96.9 GW — **massive 11 GW divergence between models**. Which is right determines whether the evening ramp delivers.
2. **Wind is the critical variable again.** Meteo forecasts wind dropping from 5,929 → 2,068 MW by HE20. Yesterday wind was 2,800 MW at HE20 and the ramp still only hit $122 West. **If wind drops to 2,068 with 119 GW load, the ramp could be the week's strongest.** But the 119 GW load forecast may be too high based on Meteo's 108 GW read.
3. **Overnight N-S congestion was historic.** HE1 Eastern -$129 congestion. The overnight heating load buildup under Bedington + Graceton is creating extreme pre-dawn N-S pressure. **This is the peak congestion stress — Graceton returns 3/20, Hosensac 3/19, multiple 345 kV lines 3/20.** Today and tomorrow are the last days of peak constraint pressure.
4. **DA at $90 West is pricing another big day** — but yesterday DA at $90.50 overpriced by $35. The market has overpriced 4 consecutive days. NxtDay DA traded up to $101.95 for today — market is aggressively long the Wednesday setup.
5. **MISO unscheduled at -3,948** — biggest of the week. This could amplify Western congestion and is a bearish signal for Chicago Hub. Watch for Chicago pricing pressure.
6. **Gas easing is a mild bearish factor** — M3 at $2.87 from $3.03 peak. AGT from $4.92 → $4.62. Takes ~$1.50/MWh off the marginal gas unit vs Monday.

### What Matters Today
1. **Morning ramp is already extreme** — HE7 West $127.80, Dom $145.03. Eastern at $31 with -$86 congestion. N-S flows under Conastone/Graceton outages + cold-driven heating load = massive congestion. This is what Edi flagged: "strong Graceton" with wind dipping into morning ramp.
2. **Evening ramp is the main event** — Meteo price forecast: **Dom HE20 $223.90, HE21 $200.04, System $197.64.** Solar cliff: 9,989 → 306 MW over 6 hours. Load forecast 113,851 peak. All three ingredients from 3/12 ($889 HE20) are back — but now with even higher load and gas. DA cleared West at $90.50 — if Meteo is even close, DART will be massive.
3. **Gas jumped and is now a driver** — M3 at $3.03 vs $2.47 last week. +$0.56 raises the marginal gas unit cost. AGT at $4.92 shows NE gas stress. This changes the stack — gas units that were cheap last week are now more expensive.
4. **Wind is fading** — 8,271 MW this morning vs 9,300+ yesterday. Edi flagged the wind dip. If wind drops through the afternoon into the evening ramp, the stack loses its biggest cushion right when solar is also disappearing.
5. **Outages dropped 3.6 GW** — 42,149 MW total, forced down to 9,487. Some units returning. This is the one bearish offset — more capacity available. But 42 GW offline + 114 GW load + solar cliff + wind fading = still very tight.
6. **ECMWF ensemble widening HE17-18** (5,370 MW spread) — afternoon solar cliff timing is uncertain. If solar drops faster than forecast, the evening ramp starts earlier and harder.

### NOTES

- Gridstatus

Outages are expected to amplify systemic N-S congestion at the start of next week.

The Conastone 500/230kV XF outage is scheduled to begin at the start of the day, which, combined with ongoing line work on Conastone - Northwest and Graceton - Manor, is likely to increase N-S flows. Sustained output from run-of-river hydro generation at units like Conowingo will also amplify risk.

Beyond the increased outage and hydro risk, models indicate a cold shift across the East coast, driving heating load risks, particularly during the middle of the week, which could drive rounds of bullish congestion over the morning and evening peaks.

One mitigating factor is the expected return of Calvert Cliffs. The unit began its 27-day outage on February 16th, which puts it on track for a return over the weekend, barring any extension. The return of sink-side, baseload generation will help bolster the PEPCO stack and may help to moderate N-S congestion, though likely not enough over the peak.

- Gridstatus

Explosive pricing emerged in PJM this morning as cold temperatures drove sustained demand overperformance.

Temperatures across the RTO dipped below freezing, including electric heating-rich Virginia. This load overperformance came at the same time as the RTO has over 45 GW of generation offline, compounding the RTO's challenge of balancing flows and potentially driving higher-priced units to be dispatched.

Risks during shoulder season are increasing as an influx of flat load upends typical demand trends, complicating operations as transmission and generation outages spike.

#### Notes

- Gristatus

Internal scheduled capacity points to additional N-S congestion risks this afternoon.

The Mid-Atlantic generation premium, relative to the South, has increased today, driven primarily by a drop in South generation. Additionally, this premium is likely ignoring the increase in generation at Hope Creek, which is likely not DA committed as it ramps up from outage.

Beyond the bullish generation setup, demand still points to afternoon risks in the South as load over the mid to late afternoon picks up, while Mid-A load is expected to just begin pushing out of an afternoon trough.

The DA did pick up on more of this congestion risk compared to yesterday, though based on the real-time strength we saw yesterday, and PJM's continued struggles accounting for the later DST peak, we could see another round of volatility this evening

- Gristatus

Congestion has been firing off in Southern PJM this morning, with mixed Dominion zonal impacts.

A combination of Aquia Harbor - Garinsoville and Nottingham SD has been plaguing the region throughout the morning, driven by a combination of differentiating load curves and increasingly likely solar curtailments.

While Aquia Harbor congestion is more neutral to the Dominion Zone, it is decidedly bearish to Dominion Hub, which is home to a sizeable chunk of the region's solar capacity. This appears to be driving some curtailments, although it's possible some of these intervals of reduced generation are a result of cloud coverage in the West.

The loss of this solar generation, combined with a more bullish demand and generation setup, could be behind such strong congestion in PJM's most complex zone.

- Gristatus

The SPC has upped its outlook, issuing a level 4 risk for portions of northeastern IL and IN.

Unsettled weather is expected in the area, fueled in part by wide temperature spreads in the area. A stationary front is in place across Northern Illinois, and onshore winds from Lake Michigan are suppressing daytime temperatures. Observed temperatures at Midway are in the low 40s, while nearby Morris, located to the southwest, is 70.

Apart from the risk of storm-related damage, these systems would likely be bullish for prices, as the impact of reduced solar and increased lighting load will offset any bearish impact from reduced cooling load this early in the Spring.

- Gristatus

Considerably bearish COMED congestion was captured in the 3/11 PJM DA clear.

Tomorrow is expected to see a classic shoulder season cold frontal passage set up, with mild weather on the back side of the front, while unsettled conditions prop up load on the leading edge. In addition to an increased demand setup, wind generation in Western PJM is expected to increase tomorrow.

DA MCCs dipped as low as -$25.89/MWh over the evening peak, though this will likely not be enough to limit RT volatility as PJM struggles to capture DST impacts and light cooling load in Eastern PJM.

- Gridstatus DST Load Forecast

PJM has revised its bal-day forecast to account for a later demand peak this evening.

Forecasts released this morning have shifted the evening demand peak from 19:00 to 20:00, reflecting the later sunset, behavioral changes, and extended BTM solar contribution. This may help to push back on some volatility this evening, though we'll likely see some N-S congestion pick up as Dominion solar drops.

PJM has not made these same forecast adjustments in its DA forecast for tomorrow, which could set the stage for this volatility risk to continue.

- Gridstatus DST

Daylight Saving Time looks to be behind last night's strongly negative PJM DART.

PJM's five-minute demand heavily outperformed last night and notably peaked well after the RTO's forecast. PJM's forecast had demand peaking ~7:10 PM, just a few minutes later than the prior day, seeming to ignore that sunsets on 3/8 were almost a full hour later.

As I warned on Friday, forecasts often do not account for the shifted demand peak, leading to overperformance later in the evening. This overperformance, and particularly in Dominion, led to both energy price overperformance and bullish rounds of Nottingham SD congestion.

- Gridstatus Hope Creek

gun ramping up from its trip, which occurred at the end of last month.

The PSEG plant sits on the source of N-S congestion flowing into the DMV, though mild conditions this week will likely limit the risk of these flows manifesting. Its main impact will likely be on power prices and helping to add additional baseload capacity as the region kicks into outage season.

The trip itself is currently the subject of a special NRC investigation, looking into the drivers behind the plant trip, which happened to have occurred during last month's blizzard.

- Gridstatus Hope Creek on Mar 4th - https://www.gridstatus.io/insights/37838225657

Yesterday, the NRC announced an investigation into the unplanned outage at Hope Creek, which occurred during last month's East Coast blizzard.

The Unit, which remains offline, suffered an unplanned loss of off-site power, which lines up with an unplanned outage at the Hope Creek - Salem 500kV line. We'll continue to keep an eye on when this unit ramps back up from outage and when the full NRC report is released.

Additional outages on the Ladysmith network are likely to complicate Dominion flows.

More line work is expected to take place starting tomorrow morning on the Ladysmith 230kV network, including breaker and transformer work. In addition to this outage, work is expected to begin on Monday on the Ladysmith - Possum Point 500kV line, reducing access into power hungry Nortern Virginia.

Outages in this area, as well as impacts from constraints like Ladysmith CB, can be a bit tricky, as many nodes north of the constraint see considerable upside, while DOM zonal prices can see some slight downside, though I'd still expect to see Dominion Hub draw the short straw again.

We should see some congestion risk start to fade next week as outages return to service and Calvert Cliffs starts to ramp up at the end of the week, but spring has many rounds of expected Dominion congestion this season.

### Thurs Mar 5th

#### Price View

- DA

- Weeklies

#### Units
#### Outages

- Outage near bath: PJm should carry more reserves to help with peaking
- Ladysmith outage: Should reduce S-N flows from gas plants in South Dom, Will compete with Solar

#### Notes

- Gridstatus

Two notable Dominion line outages returned to service ahead of schedule, which could limit some Dominion congestion today.

ICI - Chickahominy and Gordonsville - Louisa CT were both completed early yesterday, with the Chickahominy outage ending, helping to reduce the risk of Harrowgate - Locks in particular.

The DOM stack is in a healthier position today as well, with an increase in capacity and a drop in peak load forecast, which could help to push back on both S-N flows and Nottingham congestion over the evening peak.

- Gridstatus

While not as extreme as yesterday's congestion so far, another bearish constraint has emerged in Southern Virginia this morning.

Bremo - Fork Union began to bind during HE 10 this morning, likely driven by the start of an intraday line outage on Clays Mill - Sedge Hill. In addition to this line outage, solar generation in Southern VA is on the source, and both Bath County and Smith Mountain, two pumped-hydro plants, are on the sink.

Pumped hydro units tend to follow set patterns, often pumping (consuming power) during periods of low demand, like the evening and daytime, and generating during the peak. These units are likely not generating, given the time of day, though I'd be surprised to see them pumping at the moment. If these units do begin to pump during the afternoon, I'd expect volatility here to increase.

- EA

Geopolitical risk premium lifts PJM-W summer sparks with limited fundamental basis

PJM-W NQ 26 spark spreads settled $4.64/MWh higher w/w yesterday, on the back of the broader geopolitical risk premium supporting global gas and coal prices. We maintain that PJM-W summer sparks are overvalued at over $69/MWh, with fair value closer to $46/MWh.

NQ 26 delivered M3 forwards rose in tandem with fixed gas, indicating the nearly $5.50/MWh rally in West Hub forwards is largely positioning-driven. CFTC data show that PJM-W ICE contract open interest is significantly higher y/y, implying more speculation or hedging activity. The summer has traded over $9/MWh higher since the beginning of Winter Storm Fern and would be a record in realisation.

Higher coal prices are also a lingering risk for summer as the 20% w/w rise in the TTF incentivises higher US exports into the Atlantic basin.

##### Gridstatus - Conastone
Outages on the Conastone network, including the parallel Conastone - Northwest line, have driven stronger N-S congestion this morning.

Conastone - Northwest has bound heavily this morning, driving notable Western Hub volatility. Beyond these line outages, the generation set up for congestion remains in place, with Calvert Cliffs still on outage on the sink. Dominion load has come in relatively strong this morning as well, as cloud coverage has extended the morning peak.

Some upside risks continue throughout the day, as cloud coverage is expected to suppress solar generation in Dominion over the daytime, though these same demand risks are in place on the source. These outages are expected for much of the month, keeping some upside risks in place particuraly over the morning ramp and on cloudy days.

##### EA - Hope Creek emergency shutdown
Hope Creek emergency shutdown could offset expected 0.5 GW y/y rise in spring PJM nuclear generation

We model PJM’s nuclear generation will average 0.5 GW higher over March–May due to lower refuelling outages, but there is downside risk to our forecast if Hope Creek’s (PSEG; 1.2 GW) emergency shutdown is prolonged. Hope Creek conducted a hot shutdown on 23 February at 2:30 am due to a loss of grid power during extreme weather. The event was declared over by the afternoon, but the unit has not returned to service. The reactor operates on an 18-month refuelling cycle and last refuelled in autumn 2025, so it is unlikely that the unit is currently refuelling.

Reductions to nuclear generation would moderately raise spring PJM fossil call beyond our expectations. We expect most of this increase to be served by gas generation given April–May dispatch costs for CCGTs burning M3 gas are over $5/MWh cheaper than that of coal plants burning NAPP coal, but current geopolitical uncertainty may have knock-on effects for forward fixed gas prices.

##### Gridstatus
PJM saw multiple nuclear refueling outages and a return this weekend.

Two units appear to have begun refueling outages, Davis Besse and Byron 1 . Beyond upward pressure on energy prices, these constraints will have congestion impacts in ATSI and COMED, respectively.

The loss of Davis Besse in Northwest Ohio keeps pressure on flows from Michigan into Ohio, responsible for constraints like Monroe - Lallendorf, which has impacts on both PJM and MISO. Staying in the same M2M constraint lane, the loss of Byron somewhat reduces risk on bearish COMED, bullish INDY, West to East congestion.

Offsetting some of the impact of the loss of Byron is the return of LaSalle 1, which was the first PJM nuke to go on outage. LaSalle ramped up from outage over the weekend, offsetting some of the drop in the larger Byron unit

##### Gridstatus
March is expected to come in like a lion in the Mid-Atlantic, driving icing risk across central PA tomorrow.

Unsettled weather is expected across the region tomorrow, bringing low-level cloud coverage and precipitation. BTM solar generation is expected to be limited, driving upward pressure on daytime prices.

Beyond load pressure, some icing risk is expected across central PA, which could lead to wind curtailments. The price impacts from any curtailments should be limited, given how weak wind generation is expected to be to begin with, though any lost generation would likely come at the same time as Mid-A load is overperforming.

##### Gridstatus
Multiple outages on the Elmont 500kV and Chesterfield 230kV network complicate flows in Central VA today.

Central Virginia is no stranger to complex power flows, a challenge made only worse by the growth of data centers in and around Richmond and the expansion of solar along the VA/NC border.

Outages on the Elmont 50o0kV network are expected to begin today and last throughout the month, while the Hopewell - Chesterfield outage is expected to last into mid June (though some line work here is expected to be out through the end of the month.

Impacts could be felt due to load levels, though the expected increase in source-side solar generation on Wednesday will drive stronger S-N congestion risk, likely sending downside to Dominion Hub.

#### Chat w/ Edi — AEP Constraint & Wind/Solar Dynamics
- **AEP constraint discussion:** Questioned whether the Hyatt-Marysville constraint should put upward pressure on cash despite a weak shift factor for West Hub. Concluded it felt stronger than the shift factor implied, but outage was expected to end that day.
- **Supply stack:** Load 10 GW lower DoD with weaker commitment. Decent solar, steady gas, coal ramping down — mostly outage-driven and weaker commitment.
- **Wind → congestion dynamics:** Strong wind is bearish Chicago. When wind drops, west-to-east flows should ease — which would *alleviate* the west-to-east constraint (Aidan initially had this backwards).
- **Solar ramp + wind drop:** Two-fold effect — alleviates congestion but raises the question of what happens to energy. A strong solar ramp with wind dropping is bearish for energy.
- **Valley pricing:** Energy around $27–32 for the valley; gas in the money at $3 Z5/M3 → expect energy to soften. Ohio gas plants even cheaper.
- **Takeaway:** The constraint is a typical west-to-east wind-driven one. Nukes and wind zones are the key drivers on that flow path.
